Reaction No. 5926
2<Cys-2> + Hg+2 = Hg+2_Cys-2(2)

Note: Literature is all over the place. The study of Koszegi-Szalai & Paal Talanta,




                                         – Page 44 of 349 –
JESS Thermodynamic Database v8.9                                                Mercury


1999, 48, 393 [99KoP_7680] for Hg-Penicillamine seems most authoritative and is used
to anchor all assessments for Cys-2 & GSH-3. These lgKs may seem to follow Bassinger
et al. [81BCJ_4628] who have K1 = 37.8, K2 = 6.2 and so B120 = 44.0; Neikovskii et al
have K1 = 43.7 Stricks & Kolthoff have K1 = 43.6; but Lenz & Martell have K1 = 14.2
Note that the proton cannot compete with Hg+2 so MGL alone no good. Without more to
go on, I prefer B110 = too low to get and B120 = 40 odd for all three ligands.

                                         Data Assessment


Weight                          Assessment
9            highest accuracy
8            multi-determined; excellent dependability
7            trustworthy; outstanding single determination
6            better than average reliability
5            average single determination
4            some doubt
3            poorly known
2            guess to achieve consistency (or just as bad)
1            no information but consistent
0            problematic/inconsistent




                                             Techniques


Abbrev                      Method
CMN          Several experimental values (crit.)
CRV          Critical review




                                             – Page 324 of 349 –
JESS Thermodynamic Database v8.9                              Mercury


CSM    Smith & Martell Vols 1-6 (crit.)
EAE    Automated extrapolation
EBP    By Proxy
EDH    Debye-Hueckel corrections
EES    Personal estimate
EFE    Free Energy relations
EIU    Critical IUPAC review (estim.)
ELC    Linear Combination of Reactions
EMU    Method unknown
ENS    Not specified
EOD    Calculated from data of others
EOR    Other Reaction Constants
ESC    Standard conditions anchor
ESL    Similar Ligand
MAG    Silver electrode e.m.f.
MAX    Anion exchange
MCE    Cation exchange
MCL    Calorimetry
MCN    Conductivity
MCV    Cyclic voltammetry
MDG    Combination of Thermodynamic Data
MDS    Distribution between two phases
MEF    Electromotoric force, not specified
MEP    Electrophoresis
MGC    Gas chromatography
MGL    Glass electrode
MHG    Emf with amalgam electrode
MHY    Emf with hydrogen electrode
MIS    Ion selective electrode
MIX    Ion exchange
MKN    Rate of reaction
MMR    Nuclear magnetic resonance
MMX    Mixed techniques
MPH    pH method, not specified
MPL    Polarography
MPM    Polarimetry

MSL    Solubility
